     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Design_and_development">
       Design and development
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Design and development">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Embraer_EMB_312_Tucano#Development" title="Embraer EMB 312 Tucano">
       Development of the EMB-312 Tucano
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      During the mid-1980s Embraer was working on the
      <a href="/wiki/Short_Tucano" title="Short Tucano">
       Short Tucano
      </a>
      alongside a new version designed EMB-312G1, carrying the same Garrett engine. The EMB-312G1 prototype flew for the first time in July 1986. However, the project was dropped because the Brazilian Air Force was not interested in it. Nonetheless, the lessons from recent combat use of the aircraft in Peru and Venezuela led Embraer to keep up the studies. Besides a trainer, it researched a helicopter attack version designed "Helicopter killer" or EMB-312H.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The study was stimulated by the unsuccessful bid for the US military
      <a href="/wiki/Joint_Primary_Aircraft_Training_System" title="Joint Primary Aircraft Training System">
       Joint Primary Aircraft Training System
      </a>
      (JPATS) program. A proof-of-concept prototype, the PT-ZTW flew for the first time in September 1991, the aircraft features a 1.37-meter (4.49-ft) fuselage extension with the addition of sections before and after of the cockpit to restore its center of gravity and stability, a strengthened airframe, cockpit pressurization and stretched nose to house the more powerful
      <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney_Canada_PT6" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney Canada PT6">
       PT6A-67R
      </a>
      (1,424
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaft_horsepower" title="Shaft horsepower">
       Shp
      </a>
      ) engine. Two new prototypes with the PT6A-68A (1,250
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaft_horsepower" title="Shaft horsepower">
       Shp
      </a>
      ) engine were built in 1993. The second prototype flew for the first time in May 1993 and the third prototype flew in October 1993.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forecast_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Forecast-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EMB-312H_PT-ZTW.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="1024" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/EMB-312H_PT-ZTW.jpg/220px-EMB-312H_PT-ZTW.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/EMB-312H_PT-ZTW.jpg/330px-EMB-312H_PT-ZTW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/EMB-312H_PT-ZTW.jpg/440px-EMB-312H_PT-ZTW.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EMB-312H_PT-ZTW.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        This EMB-312H Prototype first flew in 9 September 1991, currently is on display at the Memorial Aeroespacial Brasileiro in
        <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_dos_Campos" title="So Jos dos Campos">
         So Jos dos Campos
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The request for a light attack aircraft was part of the Brazilian government's
      <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Surveillance_System" title="Amazon Surveillance System">
       SIVAM (Amazon Surveillance System)
      </a>
      Project. This aircraft would fly with the
      <a href="/wiki/Embraer_R-99" title="Embraer R-99">
       R-99A
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Embraer_R-99" title="Embraer R-99">
       R-99B
      </a>
      aircraft then in service and be used to intercept illegal aircraft flights and patrol Brazil's borders. The ALX Project was then created by the Brazilian Air Force, which was also in need of a military trainer to replace the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embraer_EMB_326GB_Xavante" title="Embraer EMB 326GB Xavante">
       Embraer EMB 326GB Xavante
      </a>
      . The new aircraft was to be suited to the Amazon region (high temperature, moisture, and precipitation; low threat). The ALX was then specified as a
      <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">
       turboprop
      </a>
      engine aircraft with a long range and autonomy, able to operate in night and day, in any meteorological conditions, and able to land on short airfields lacking infrastructure.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norris_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Norris-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 1995, the Brazilian Ministry of Aeronautics awarded Embraer a $50 million contract for ALX development. Two
      <a href="/wiki/Embraer_EMB_312_Tucano" title="Embraer EMB 312 Tucano">
       EMB-312H
      </a>
      were updated to serve as ALX prototypes. These made their initial flights in their new configuration in 1996 and 1997, respectively. The initial flight of a production-configured ALX, further modified from one of the prototypes, occurred in 2 June 1999. The second prototype brought up to two-seater configuration and performing its first flight on 22 October 1999. The changes had been so considerable that the type was given a new designation, the "EMB-314 Super Tucano".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forecast_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Forecast-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The total cost of the aircraft development was quoted to be between US$200 millions and US$300 millions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The aircraft differs from the baseline
      <a href="/wiki/Embraer_EMB_312_Tucano" title="Embraer EMB 312 Tucano">
       EMB-312 Tucano
      </a>
      trainer aircraft in several respects. It is powered by a more powerful 1,600
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaft_horsepower" title="Shaft horsepower">
       Shp
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney_Canada_PT6" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney Canada PT6">
       Pratt &amp; Whitney Canada PT6A-68C
      </a>
      engine (compared to the EMB-312's 750
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaft_horsepower" title="Shaft horsepower">
       Shp
      </a>
      powerplant); has a strengthened airframe to sustain higher g loads and increase fatigue life to 18,00012,000 hours in operational environments; a reinforced landing gear to handle greater takeoff weights and heavier stores load, up to 1,550 kilograms (3,300 pounds); Kevlar armour protection; two internal wing-mounted .50 calibre machine guns (with 200 rounds of ammunition each);
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      capacity to carry various ordnance on five weapon hardpoints including Giat NC621 20mm cannon pods, Mk 81/82 bombs,
      <a href="/wiki/MAA-1_Piranha" title="MAA-1 Piranha">
       MAA-1 Piranha
      </a>
      air-to-air missiles (AAMs), BLG-252 cluster bombs and SBAT-70/19 or LAU-68A/G rocket pods on its underwing stations; and has a night-vision goggle (NVG)-compatible "glass cockpit" with hands-on-throttle-and-stick (HOTAS) controls; provision for a datalink; a video camera and recorder; an embedded mission-planning capability; forward-looking infrared (FLIR); chaff/flare dispensers; missile approach warning receiver systems (MAWS) and radar warning receivers (RWRs); zero-zero ejection seats.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The structure is corrosion-protected and the side-hinged canopy has a windshield able to withstand
      <a href="/wiki/Bird_strike" title="Bird strike">
       bird strike
      </a>
      impacts up to 270 kts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A-29A_Super_Tucano_Rob_Schleiffert.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="933" data-file-width="1400" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/A-29A_Super_Tucano_Rob_Schleiffert.jpg/220px-A-29A_Super_Tucano_Rob_Schleiffert.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/A-29A_Super_Tucano_Rob_Schleiffert.jpg/330px-A-29A_Super_Tucano_Rob_Schleiffert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/A-29A_Super_Tucano_Rob_Schleiffert.jpg/440px-A-29A_Super_Tucano_Rob_Schleiffert.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A-29A_Super_Tucano_Rob_Schleiffert.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The A-29A incorporates an additional tank for 400 liters of fuel.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1996, Embraer selected the Israeli firm
      <a href="/wiki/Elbit_Systems" title="Elbit Systems">
       Elbit Systems
      </a>
      to supply the mission avionics for the ALX. For this contract, Elbit was chosen over
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GEC-Marconi" title="GEC-Marconi">
       GEC-Marconi
      </a>
      and Sextant Avionique. The Israeli company supplies such equipment as the mission computer, head-up displays, and navigation and stores management systems.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 13 October 2010, the Super Tucano A-29B had passed the mark of 48,000 hours since 21 July 2005 on full scale wing-fuselage structural fatigue test, conducted by the Aeronautical Systems Division (ASA), part of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_General_Command_for_Aerospace_Technology#Aeronautics_and_Space_Institute_.28IAE.29" title="Brazilian General Command for Aerospace Technology">
       Aeronautics and Space Institute
      </a>
      (IAE) at the Structural Testing Laboratory. The test involves a complex system of hydraulics and tabs that apply pressure to aircraft structure, simulating air pressure from flying at varying altitudes. The simulation continued for another year to complete the engine fatigue life test and crack propagation studies for a damage tolerance analysis program of conducted by
      <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">
       Embraer
      </a>
      and IAE/ASA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Embraer developed an advanced training and support system suite called Training Operational Support System (TOSS) an integrated computational tool composed of four systems: Computer Based Training (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E-learning#Computer-based_training" title="E-learning">
       CBT
      </a>
      ) enabling the student to rehearse the next sortie on a computer simulation; Aviation Mission Planning Station (AMPS) which uses the 3D visuals to practice planned missions and to check inter-visibility between aircraft and from aircraft and other entities; Mission Debriefing Station (MDS) employs real aircraft data to playback missions for review and analysis;
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flight_Simulator" title="Flight Simulator">
       Flight Simulator
      </a>
      (FS).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      MPS and MDS was enhanced with MAKs 3D visualization solution to support airforces pre-existing data, including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GIS" title="GIS">
       GIS
      </a>
      , Web-based servers and a plug-in for custom terrain formats.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mak_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-mak-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2012,
      <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Defense,_Space_%26_Security" title="Boeing Defense, Space &amp; Security">
       Boeing Defense, Space &amp; Security
      </a>
      was selected to integrate
      <a href="/wiki/Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition" title="Joint Direct Attack Munition">
       Joint Direct Attack Munition
      </a>
      (JDAM) and
      <a href="/wiki/Small_Diameter_Bomb" title="Small Diameter Bomb">
       Small Diameter Bombs
      </a>
      (SDB) for the Super Tucano.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2013, Embraer Defense and Security
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CEO" title="CEO">
       CEO
      </a>
      disclosed that its subsidiary, OrbiSat, was developing a new radar for the Super Tucano.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A Colombian General disclosed that the future
      <a href="/wiki/Side_looking_airborne_radar" title="Side looking airborne radar">
       Side looking airborne radar
      </a>
      (SLAR) will be able to locate ground targets smaller than a car with digital precision.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_history">
       Operational history
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Operational history">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">
       Brazil
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Brazil">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EDA_Super_Tucano.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2589" data-file-width="4771" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/EDA_Super_Tucano.jpg/220px-EDA_Super_Tucano.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/EDA_Super_Tucano.jpg/330px-EDA_Super_Tucano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/EDA_Super_Tucano.jpg/440px-EDA_Super_Tucano.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EDA_Super_Tucano.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Smoke_Squadron" title="Smoke Squadron">
         Smoke Squadron
        </a>
        EMB-314
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In August 2001, the
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Air_Force" title="Brazilian Air Force">
       Brazilian Air Force
      </a>
      awarded Embraer a contract for 76 Super Tucano / ALX aircraft with options for a further 23. A total of 99 aircraft were acquired from a contract estimated to be worth around $214.1 USD millions, 66 of these aircraft are two seater versions, designated A-29B. The remaining 33 aircraft are the single seat A-29 ALX version.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-investe_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-investe-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first aircraft was delivered in December 2003. By September 2007, 50 aircraft had entered service.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The 99th, and last, aircraft was delivered in June 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      One of the main missions of the aircraft is border patrol under the
      <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Surveillance_System" title="Amazon Surveillance System">
       SIVAM
      </a>
      programme. On 3 June 2009, two Brazilian Air Force Super Tucanos, guided by an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embraer_E-99" title="Embraer E-99">
       Embraer E-99
      </a>
      , intercepted an
      <a href="/wiki/Cessna_206" title="Cessna 206">
       Cessna U206G
      </a>
      engaged in drug trafficking activities. Inbound from
      <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">
       Bolivia
      </a>
      , the Cessna was intercepted in the region of
      <a href="/wiki/Alta_Floresta_d%27Oeste" title="Alta Floresta d'Oeste">
       Alta Floresta d'Oeste
      </a>
      and, after exhausting all procedures, one of the Super Tucanos fired a warning shot from its 12.7mm machine guns, after which the aircraft followed the Super Tucanos to
      <a href="/wiki/Cacoal" title="Cacoal">
       Cacoal
      </a>
      airport. This incident was the first use of powers granted under the Shoot-Down Act, which was enacted in October 2004 in order to legislate for the downing of illegal flights. A total of 176kg of pure
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cocaine_base_paste" title="Cocaine base paste">
       cocaine base paste
      </a>
      , enough to produce almost a
      <a href="/wiki/Ton" title="Ton">
       ton
      </a>
      of cocaine, was discovered on board the Cessna; the aircraft's two occupants attempted a ground escape before being arrested by
      <a href="/wiki/Federal_Police_Department" title="Federal Police Department">
       Federal Police
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Pimenta_Bueno" title="Pimenta Bueno">
       Pimenta Bueno
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Operation_.C3.81gata">
       Operation gata
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Operation gata">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      On 5 August 2011, Brazil started
      <i>
       Operation gata
      </i>
      , part of a major "Frontiers Strategic Plan" launched in June, with almost 30 continuous days of rigorous military activity in the region of Brazils border with Colombia, it mobilized 35 aircraft and more than 3,000 military personnel of the
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army" title="Brazilian Army">
       Brazilian Army
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Navy" title="Brazilian Navy">
       Brazilian Navy
      </a>
      and Brazilian Air Force surveillance against drug trafficking, illegal mining and logging, and trafficking of wild animals. A-29s of 1 / 3  Aviation Group (GAV), Squadron Scorpion, launched a strike upon an illicit airstrip, deploying eight 230kg (500lb) computer-guided
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_82_bomb" title="Mark 82 bomb">
       Mk 82 bombs
      </a>
      to render the airstrip unusable.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Multiple
      <a href="/wiki/Elbit_Hermes_450" title="Elbit Hermes 450">
       RQ-450
      </a>
      UAVs were assigned for night operations, locating remote jungle airstrips used by drug smuggling gangs along the border. The UAVs were typically guarded by several E-99 aircraft. The
      <a href="/wiki/Elbit_Hermes_450" title="Elbit Hermes 450">
       RQ-450
      </a>
      located targets for the A-29 Super Tucanos, allowing them to bomb the airstrips with an extremely high level of accuracy, making use of
      <a href="/wiki/Night_vision" title="Night vision">
       night-vision
      </a>
      systems and
      <a href="/wiki/Constantly_computed_impact_point" title="Constantly computed impact point">
       computer systems calculating the impact points of munitions
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 15 September 2011, Brazil launched the
      <i>
       Operation gata 2
      </i>
      on the borders with
      <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">
       Uruguay
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
       Argentina
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">
       Paraguay
      </a>
      . Part of this border is the infamous
      <a href="/wiki/Triple_Frontier" title="Triple Frontier">
       Triple Frontier
      </a>
      . A-29s from
      <a href="/wiki/Maring%C3%A1" title="Maring">
       Maring
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dourados" title="Dourados">
       Dourados
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Campo_Grande" title="Campo Grande">
       Campo Grande
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Northrop_F-5#Brazil" title="Northrop F-5">
       Brazilian upgraded
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Northrop_F-5" title="Northrop F-5">
       Northrop F-5 Tiger II/F-5EMs
      </a>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Canoas" title="Canoas">
       Canoas
      </a>
      , intercepted a total of 33 aircraft during
      <i>
       Operation gata 2
      </i>
      in this area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Brazilian forces had seized 62 tons of narcotics, made 3,000 arrests and destroyed three illicit airstrips, while over 650 tons of weapons and explosives have been seized.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 22 November 2011, Brazil launched the
      <i>
       Operation gata 3
      </i>
      on the borders with
      <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">
       Bolivia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
       Peru
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">
       Paraguay
      </a>
      . It involved 6,500 personnel, backed by 10 ships and 200 land patrol vehicles, in addition to 70 aircraft, including fighter, transport and reconnaissance aircraft. This was the largest Brazilian coordinated action involving the Army, Navy and Air Force against illegal trafficking and organized crime, along a border strip of almost 7,000km.
      <a href="/wiki/AMX_International_AMX" title="AMX International AMX">
       A-1(AMX)
      </a>
      , Northrop F-5 Tiger II/ F-5EM and A-29 Super Tucanos from
      <a href="/wiki/Tabatinga" title="Tabatinga">
       Tabatinga
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Campo_Grande" title="Campo Grande">
       Campo Grande
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cuiab%C3%A1" title="Cuiab">
       Cuiab
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Vilhena" title="Vilhena">
       Vilhena
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Porto_Velho" title="Porto Velho">
       Porto Velho
      </a>
      were employed in defending air space, supported by
      <a href="/wiki/Airborne_early_warning_and_control" title="Airborne early warning and control">
       AEW&amp;C
      </a>
      s
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embraer_E-99" title="Embraer E-99">
       E-99
      </a>
      , equipped with a 250km range radar capable of detecting low flying aircraft, and
      <a href="/wiki/Embraer_R-99" title="Embraer R-99">
       R-99
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Remote_sensing" title="Remote sensing">
       remote sensing
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Surveillance_aircraft" title="Surveillance aircraft">
       surveillance
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 7 December 2011, Brazilian
      <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Brazil)" title="Ministry of Defence (Brazil)">
       Ministry of Defence
      </a>
      informed the nation that drug seizures were up by 1,319% over the last six months, compared to prior six months.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">
       Chile
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Chile">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FACh_-_Super_Tucano.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/FACh_-_Super_Tucano.jpg/220px-FACh_-_Super_Tucano.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/FACh_-_Super_Tucano.jpg/330px-FACh_-_Super_Tucano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/FACh_-_Super_Tucano.jpg/440px-FACh_-_Super_Tucano.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FACh_-_Super_Tucano.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Air_Force" title="Chilean Air Force">
         Chilean Air Force
        </a>
        EMB-314
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In August 2008 the
      <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Air_Force" title="Chilean Air Force">
       Chilean Air Force
      </a>
      signed a contract valued at $120 millions for 12 A-29B.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The contract includes a broad Integrated Logistic Support (ILS) package and an advanced Training and Operation Support System (TOSS), covering not only the aircraft, but also an integrated suite for ground support stations. The FACHs TOSS consists of three systems: a Mission Planning Station (MPS) in which instructor and student program all phases of flight, setting the various parameters of each phase along with navigation, communications, goals and simulations; a Mission Debriefing Station (MDS) empowering students with the ability to review all and each flight aspects and phases, enabling to look at the errors and correct them for their next mission; and a Flight Simulator (FS).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first four aircraft arrived in December 2009, with the remaining deliveries taking place on March, April and May of the following year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RAsas_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-RAsas-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The aircraft are based at Los Cndores Air Base (45km from
      <a href="/wiki/Iquique" title="Iquique">
       Iquique
      </a>
      ) and are used for tactical instruction at the 1st Air Brigade for the Aviation Group #1,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the fully digital cockpit allow students to do a smooth transition between
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-35_Pill%C3%A1n" title="T-35 Pilln">
       T-35 Pilln
      </a>
      (basic trainer) to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-16" title="F-16">
       F-16
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RAsas_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-RAsas-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">
       Colombia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Colombia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A-29_SuperTucano.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/A-29_SuperTucano.JPG/220px-A-29_SuperTucano.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/A-29_SuperTucano.JPG/330px-A-29_SuperTucano.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/A-29_SuperTucano.JPG/440px-A-29_SuperTucano.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A-29_SuperTucano.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A-29 Super Tucano of the
        <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Air_Force" title="Colombian Air Force">
         Colombian Air Force
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A total of 25 Super Tucanos (variant AT-29B) were purchased by the
      <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Air_Force" title="Colombian Air Force">
       Colombian Air Force
      </a>
      in a 234 million
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">
       USD
      </a>
      deal, purchased directly from the Brazilian company Embraer. The first three aircraft arrived in the morning of 14 December 2006 to the military airfield of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CATAM" title="CATAM">
       CATAM
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogot">
       Bogot
      </a>
      . Two more aircraft were delivered on the week of 16 December 2006, 10 more in the first half of 2007 and the rest in June 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 18 January 2007, a squadron of
      <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Air_Force" title="Colombian Air Force">
       Colombian Air Force
      </a>
      Super Tucanos launched the first-ever combat mission of its type, attacking
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia">
       FARC
      </a>
      (Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia) positions in the jungle with
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_82_bomb" title="Mark 82 bomb">
       Mark 82 bombs
      </a>
      . This attack made use of the Super Tucano's
      <a href="/wiki/Constantly_computed_impact_point" title="Constantly computed impact point">
       CCIP
      </a>
      (Continuously Computed Impact Point) capability; the aircraft's performance in action was a reported success.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Embraer_Close_Contract_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Embraer_Close_Contract-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 11 July 2012, the first aircraft was lost near the Jambalo town, when the aircraft were flying in one operation against Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia (FARC), rebels claim they shot down the aircraft with .50 (12.7mm) machine gun, however, the
      <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Air_Force" title="Colombian Air Force">
       Colombian Air Force
      </a>
      challenged the rebel group's claims after inspection of the aircraft wreckage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-FARC_operations">
       Anti-FARC operations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Anti-FARC operations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In 2008, the Colombian Air Force used a Super Tucano armed with
      <a href="/wiki/Griffin_LGB" title="Griffin LGB">
       Griffin laser guided bombs
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_Colombian_raid_into_Ecuador" title="2008 Colombian raid into Ecuador">
       inside Ecuadorian airspace
      </a>
      during
      <a href="/wiki/Operacion_Fenix" title="Operacion Fenix">
       "Operation Phoenix"
      </a>
      , to destroy a guerrilla cell and kill the second-in-command chief of
      <a href="/wiki/FARC" title="FARC">
       FARC
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Reyes" title="Ral Reyes">
       Ral Reyes
      </a>
      . This event led to an
      <a href="/wiki/2008_Andean_diplomatic_crisis" title="2008 Andean diplomatic crisis">
       Andean diplomatic break
      </a>
      between the two countries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fenix_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fenix-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 21 September 2010,
      <i>
       Operation Sodoma
      </i>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Meta_Department" title="Meta Department">
       Meta department
      </a>
      began, 120 miles south of the capital
      <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogot">
       Bogot
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia">
       FARC
      </a>
      commander
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mono_Jojoy" title="Mono Jojoy">
       Mono Jojoy
      </a>
      was killed in a massive military operation in the early hours of 22 September, a
      <a href="/wiki/Squadron_(aviation)" title="Squadron (aviation)">
       squadron
      </a>
      of 25 EMB-314 launched seven tonnes of explosives on the camp, while some 600 special forces troops descended by rope from helicopters, opposed by 700 guerrillas. 20 guerrillas died in the attack.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 2 October 2010, Super Tucanos using infrared cameras spotted and bombarded the FARC 57th front in the
      <a href="/wiki/Choc%C3%B3_Department" title="Choc Department">
       Choc Department
      </a>
      during Operation Darin. The bombardment, just a kilometer away from the Panama border, killed five rebels, including several commanders.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colombian_EMB-314_flaring.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Colombian_EMB-314_flaring.jpg/220px-Colombian_EMB-314_flaring.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Colombian_EMB-314_flaring.jpg/330px-Colombian_EMB-314_flaring.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Colombian_EMB-314_flaring.jpg/440px-Colombian_EMB-314_flaring.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colombian_EMB-314_flaring.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Colombian Super Tucano deploys flares
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 15 October 2011, Operation Odiseo started with a total of 969 different military bodies of the
      <a href="/wiki/Military_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Military Forces of Colombia">
       Colombian armed forces
      </a>
      . A total of 18 aircraft participated in "Operation Odiseo". On 4 November 2011, five Super Tucanos were used to launch a heavy bombing of 100lb(45kg) and 250lb(135kg), plus high-precision smart bombs. This operation ended with the death of the leader of the Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia (Fuerzas Armadas Revolucionarias de Colombia,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia">
       FARC
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cano" title="Alfonso Cano">
       Alfonso Cano
      </a>
      . It was biggest blow in the history of the
      <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">
       guerrilla
      </a>
      organization.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At dawn of 22 February 2012, EMB-314s identified the camp of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia">
       FARC
      </a>
      's 57th Front, 15 kilometers north of
      <a href="/wiki/Bojay%C3%A1" title="Bojay">
       Bojay
      </a>
      near the border with Panama. In Operation Frontera, Super Tucanos dropped two high-precision bombs, destroying the camp and killing six FARC rebels including Pedro Alfonso Alvarado alias "Mapanao", responsible for the
      <a href="/wiki/Bojay%C3%A1_massacre" title="Bojay massacre">
       Bojay massacre
      </a>
      in 2002 which killed 119 civilians.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Espada_de_Honor_War_Plan">
       Espada de Honor War Plan
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Espada de Honor War Plan">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The Espada de Honor War Plan is an aggressive Colombian counterinsurgency strategy that aims to dismantle FARCs structure, both militarily and financially. It targets FARC leadership and is focused on eliminating the 15 most powerful economic and military fronts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During at Operacion Faran, at the dawn of 21 March 2012, five Super Tucanos bombarded the FARCs 10th Front guerrilla camp in
      <a href="/wiki/Arauca_Department" title="Arauca Department">
       Arauca
      </a>
      , near the Venezuelan border, killing 33 rebels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Five days later, on Operation Armagedn, nine Super Tucanos from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apiay_Air_Base" title="Apiay Air Base">
       Apiay Air Base
      </a>
      attacked the FARCs 27th front camp in
      <a href="/wiki/Vista_Hermosa,_Meta" title="Vista Hermosa, Meta">
       Vista Hermosa, Meta
      </a>
      , using coordinates received from a guerrilla informant recruited by the police intelligence, launching 40 guided 500 pounds bombs within three minutes, totally destroying the camp and killing 36 rebels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In late May, Super Tucanos bombarded a
      <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Army_(Colombia)" title="National Liberation Army (Colombia)">
       National Liberation Army
      </a>
      (ELN) camp located in rural Santa Rosa at
      <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Department" title="Bolvar Department">
       Bolvar Department
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 31 May 2012, a bombardment over the Western Front of the ELN at an inhospitable area of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Choco_Department" title="Choco Department">
       Choco Department
      </a>
      killed seven rebels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 6 June 2012, during a minute and half bombardment over FARC's 37th front located on northern
      <a href="/wiki/Antioquia_Department" title="Antioquia Department">
       Antioquia Department
      </a>
      , five Super Tucanos dropped 250kg bombs, killing 8 rebels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On September, Super Tucanos provided reconnaissance and
      <a href="/wiki/Close_air_support" title="Close air support">
       close air support
      </a>
      during an "OMEGA" operation, during which 7 terrorists were gunned down and 4 captured, including "Fredy Cooper", the 7th front's leader of the Public Order Company.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 5 September 2012, "Danilo Garcia," leader of the FARC's 33rd Front was killed in a bombing raid; Danilo was considered "the right hand of supreme FARC leader alias Timochenko". Intelligence indicates that the bodies of 15 guerrillas may have been buried in the bombing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Eight A-29s carried out an air strike on 27 September during Operacin Saturno at the FARC's 37th front camp in the northwest of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antioquia_department" title="Antioquia department">
       Antioquia department
      </a>
      , resulting in the death of Efrain Gonzales Ruiz aka "Pateame" leader of the 35th and 37th front, and 13 others.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In April 2013, two Super Tucanos bombarded the FARC's 59th front
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort" title="Fort">
       fort
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Serran%C3%ADa_del_Perij%C3%A1" title="Serrana del Perij">
       Serrana del Perij
      </a>
      municipality
      <a href="/wiki/Barrancas,_La_Guajira" title="Barrancas, La Guajira">
       Barrancas, La Guajira
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Dominican_Republic">
       Dominican Republic
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Dominican Republic">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dominican_Republic_Super_Tucano.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2511" data-file-width="3767" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Dominican_Republic_Super_Tucano.jpg/220px-Dominican_Republic_Super_Tucano.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Dominican_Republic_Super_Tucano.jpg/330px-Dominican_Republic_Super_Tucano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Dominican_Republic_Super_Tucano.jpg/440px-Dominican_Republic_Super_Tucano.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dominican_Republic_Super_Tucano.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A Dominican Republic A-29 pilot taxis after a mission as part of an exercise to combat illegal drug trafficking.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In August 2001, Embraer announced the signing of a contract with the
      <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">
       Dominican Republic
      </a>
      for 10 Super Tucano aircraft, to be used for pilot training,
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_security" title="Internal security">
       internal security
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Border_guard" title="Border guard">
       border patrol
      </a>
      and counter-narcotics trafficking missions. The order was reduced to eight aircraft in January 2009, for a total amount of US$93 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first two Super Tucano aircraft were delivered to the Dominican Republic on 18 December 2009. Three were delivered in June 2010 and the remaining three in October 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AirForce_Tech_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-AirForce_Tech-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In February 2011,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic_Air_Force" title="Dominican Republic Air Force">
       Dominican Republic Air Force
      </a>
      Chief of Operations, Col. Hilton Cabral stated: "since the introduction of the Super Tucano aircraft and ground-based radars, illicit air tracks into the Dominican Republic had dropped by over 80 percent."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In August 2011, the Dominican Air Force said that since taking delivery of the Super Tucanos in 2009, it has driven away drug flights to the point that they no longer enter the country's airspace.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In May 2012, the Dominican president
      <a href="/wiki/Leonel_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Leonel Fernndez">
       Leonel Fernndez
      </a>
      gave cooperative order for the army forces to support a fleet of Super Tucanos for the anti-drugs fight on
      <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">
       Haiti
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecuador">
       Ecuador
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ecuador">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Super-Tucano_Ecuador.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="853" data-file-width="1280" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Super-Tucano_Ecuador.jpg/220px-Super-Tucano_Ecuador.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Super-Tucano_Ecuador.jpg/330px-Super-Tucano_Ecuador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Super-Tucano_Ecuador.jpg/440px-Super-Tucano_Ecuador.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Super-Tucano_Ecuador.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Super Tucano
        <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Air_Force" title="Ecuadorian Air Force">
         Ecuadorian Air Force
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Air_Force" title="Ecuadorian Air Force">
       Ecuadorian Air Force
      </a>
      operates 18 Super Tucanos, they are established at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manta_Air_Base" title="Manta Air Base">
       Manta Air Base
      </a>
      in two squadrons: 2313 "Halcones" (used for border surveillance and
      <a href="/wiki/Flight_training" title="Flight training">
       flight training
      </a>
      ) and 2311 "Dragones" (used for
      <a href="/wiki/Counter-insurgency" title="Counter-insurgency">
       Counter-insurgency
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ecuadorian Super Tucanos uses the
      <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney_Canada_PT6" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney Canada PT6">
       PT-6A-68A
      </a>
      (1,300 shp) engine.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sipri2010_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sipri2010-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 23 March 2009,
      <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">
       Embraer
      </a>
      announced that negotiations over a nine-month-old agreement with the Ecuadorian air force have finally been completed. The deal covers the supply of 24 turboprop-powered Super Tucanos, with these to replace Ecuadors ageing fleet of Vietnam-era
      <a href="/wiki/Cessna_A-37_Dragonfly" title="Cessna A-37 Dragonfly">
       Cessna A-37 Dragonfly
      </a>
      strike aircraft, and help re-assert control over the countrys airspace.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In May 2010, after receiving its sixth Super Tucano from a contract worth $270 million, Ecuador announced a reduction in its order for the Embraer EMB-314 Super Tucano from 24 to 18 aircraft to release funds to buy some used
      <a href="/wiki/South_African_Air_Force" title="South African Air Force">
       South African Air Force
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Cheetah" title="Atlas Cheetah">
       Denel Cheetah C
      </a>
      fighters. By cutting its order for the EMB-314 type, the Defence Ministry says the accrued savings would allow it to purchase the secondhand Cheetahs, and bolster the air force's flagging air defence component.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">
       Indonesia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Indonesia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In late January 2010,
      <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Air_Force" title="Indonesian Air Force">
       Indonesian Air Force
      </a>
      commander Air Marshal
      <a href="/wiki/Imam_Sufaat" title="Imam Sufaat">
       Imam Sufaat
      </a>
      made it clear that
      <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
       Indonesia
      </a>
      had split the competition, designating the Embraer EMB-314 Super Tucano turboprop from
      <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
       Brazil
      </a>
      as the preferred replacement for their OV-10s. Indonesia signed a Memorandum of Understanding with Embraer at the Indo Defense 2010 exhibition in Jakarta. Indonesia ordered 8 EMB-314 Super Tucanos at first, with an option for another 8 on the same terms. The first Super Tucanos were scheduled to arrive in 2012, and the order also included ground-support stations and a logistics package. Defense Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Purnomo_Yusgiantoro" title="Purnomo Yusgiantoro">
       Purnomo Yusgiantoro
      </a>
      added that state aircraft maker
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PT_Dirgantara_Indonesia" title="PT Dirgantara Indonesia">
       PT Dirgantara Indonesia
      </a>
      would be used for maintenance work, and they also hoped Dirgantara would wind up manufacturing some parts and components. Subsequent contracts have ordered a total of 16 of these Super Tucano planes for the Tentara Nasional Indonesia - Angkatan Udara (TNI-AU),
      <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Air_Force" title="Indonesian Air Force">
       Indonesian Air Force
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      While
      <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
       Indonesia
      </a>
      could have made a unified choice to replace its
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OV-10_Bronco" title="OV-10 Bronco">
       OV-10 Bronco
      </a>
      FAC light attack and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bae_Hawk" title="Bae Hawk">
       Bae Hawk
      </a>
      Mk.53 trainer fleets with a multi-role jet, the demands of forward air control and counterinsurgency wars give slower and more stable platforms an advantage. The USAs
      <a href="/wiki/Fairchild_Republic_A-10_Thunderbolt_II" title="Fairchild Republic A-10 Thunderbolt II">
       A-10 Thunderbolt
      </a>
      /Warthog is Exhibit A in this respect, but its no longer in production. Propeller-driven options are emerging as the preferred choices and Embraer EMB-314 Super Tucano external link trainer/ FAC/ light attack turboprop has built a strong global lead.
     </p>
     <p>
      .On 10 July 2012 Indonesia ordered a 2nd set of 8 Super Tucano aircraft, along with a full flight simulator. This brings their order total to 16.
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 2012,
      <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
       Indonesia
      </a>
      received the first 4 airplanes from the initial batch of 8 aircraft ordered in November 2010. Embraer Defense delivered Indonesias first 4 Super Tucanos at a ceremony held in its facility in Gaviao Peixoto, So Paulo,
      <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
       Brazil
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Deliveries of the 2nd batch of Super Tucanos were delayed from their original schedule for more than seven months.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thejakartapost.com_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-thejakartapost.com-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ultimately in September 2014 the second batch left the factory in Brazil on their ferry flight to Malang
      <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Rachman_Saleh_Airport" title="Abdul Rachman Saleh Airport">
       Abdul Rachman Saleh Air Base
      </a>
      in East Java. Theyll be based at the Malang air base on Indonesias Java island. They are operated by Skadron Udara 21 as part of the 2nd Wing.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">
       United States
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: United States">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      One Super Tucano was purchased by a subsidiary of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackwater_Worldwide" title="Blackwater Worldwide">
       Blackwater Worldwide
      </a>
      , an American
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_military_contractor" title="Private military contractor">
       private military contracting firm
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The aircraft lacked the machine guns normally attached to the wings. In 2012, that aircraft was subsequently purchased by
      <a href="/wiki/Tactical_Air_Support,_Inc." title="Tactical Air Support, Inc.">
       Tactical Air Support, Inc.
      </a>
      of Reno, Nevada.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Super_Tucano_at_Moody.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1633" data-file-width="2700" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Super_Tucano_at_Moody.jpg/220px-Super_Tucano_at_Moody.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Super_Tucano_at_Moody.jpg/330px-Super_Tucano_at_Moody.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Super_Tucano_at_Moody.jpg/440px-Super_Tucano_at_Moody.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Super_Tucano_at_Moody.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        USA Super Tucano flying over
        <a href="/wiki/Moody_Air_Force_Base" title="Moody Air Force Base">
         Moody Air Force Base
        </a>
        as part of training program for the Afghan pilots.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2008, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">
       U.S. Navy
      </a>
      began testing the Super Tucano at the behest of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Special_Operations_Command" title="U.S. Special Operations Command">
       U.S. Special Operations Command
      </a>
      for its potential use to support special warfare operations,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      giving it the official U.S. designation
      <b>
       A-29B
      </b>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a-29b_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-a-29b-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2009, the Super Tucano was offered in a U.S. Air Force competition for 100 counterinsurgency aircraft.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 12 April 2010, Brazil signed a defensive pact that opened negotiations for the acquisition of 200 Super Tucanos by the U.S.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 16 November 2011, the
      <a href="/wiki/Beechcraft_T-6_Texan_II" title="Beechcraft T-6 Texan II">
       AT-6
      </a>
      was excluded from the
      <a href="/wiki/Light_Attack/Armed_Reconnaissance" title="Light Attack/Armed Reconnaissance">
       LAS Program
      </a>
      , effectively selecting the Super Tucano. According to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GAO" title="GAO">
       GAO
      </a>
      : "the Air Force concluded that HBDC had not adequately corrected deficiencies in its proposal... that multiple deficiencies and significant weaknesses found in HBDCs proposal make it technically unacceptable and results in unacceptable mission capability risk".
      <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Beechcraft" title="Hawker Beechcraft">
       Hawker Beechcraft
      </a>
      's protest against its exclusion was dismissed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the contract award was disputed and a stop-work was issued in January 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      For this procurement the avionics are to be supplied by
      <a href="/wiki/Elbit_Systems" title="Elbit Systems">
       Elbit Systems of America
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_Corporation" title="Sierra Nevada Corporation">
       Sierra Nevada
      </a>
      , the US-based prime contractor will be building the Super Tucano in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville" title="Jacksonville">
       Jacksonville
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">
       Florida
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/81st_Fighter_Squadron" title="81st Fighter Squadron">
       81st Fighter Squadron
      </a>
      , based at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moody_AFB" title="Moody AFB">
       Moody AFB
      </a>
      was reactivated on 15 January 2015 and will receive the aircraft and provide training to pilots and maintainers from the Afghan Air Force.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Purchased for the
      <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Air_Force" title="Afghan Air Force">
       Afghan Air Force
      </a>
      , they are planned to be turned over to them in December 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Until the A-29s are turned over to the Afghan Air Force, they will not have a fixed-wing close air support aircraft, but have armed helicopter options.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Honduras">
       Honduras
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Honduras">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 3 September 2011, the head of the
      <a href="/wiki/Honduran_Air_Force" title="Honduran Air Force">
       Honduran Air Force
      </a>
      said that Honduras was to procure four Super Tucanos.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hondweek_79-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hondweek-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 7 February 2012, ministers of Honduras government informed the Brazilian Trade Ministry the interest in acquire a lot of Super Tucanos.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, due the economic situation, the government was forced to repair the aging aircraft inventory, instead of buying eight EMB-314.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 17 October 2014 the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and International Cooperation (Secretaria de Relaciones Exteriores y Cooperacin Internacional) announced the go-ahead of acquiring two new Embraer A-29 Super Tucanos by the Fuerza Aerea Hondurena (
      <a href="/wiki/Honduran_Air_Force" title="Honduran Air Force">
       Honduran Air Force
      </a>
      ) following approval from the country's National Council for Security and Defence. Honduras had been looking to buy new Super Tucanos for several years, but until now had been unable to finance a purchase. As part of the deal six of the FAH's surviving
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embraer_Tucano" title="Embraer Tucano">
       Embraer EMB-312A Tucanos
      </a>
      , acquired in 1984, will be refurbished and upgraded by the manufacturer. Originally operated only by the Academia Militar de Aviacion at Palmerola for training they have recently been armed for counter-narcotics missions. Just three were airworthy as the Brazilian deal was signed for the aircraft to be upgraded and the other three be made airworthy again. Together with the two newly acquired Super Tucanos this will boost efforts to maintain security within the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Potential_operators">
       Potential operators
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Potential operators">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The A-29 Super Tucano will likely equip the
      <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Air_Force" title="Afghan Air Force">
       Afghan Air Force
      </a>
      in the light attack and advanced training role. The aircraft was declared the winner of the US Light Air Support (LAS) contract competition over the
      <a href="/wiki/Beechcraft_T-6_Texan_II" title="Beechcraft T-6 Texan II">
       Hawker Beechcraft AT-6B Texan II
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However the contract was canceled citing concerns with the procurement process.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      And rewon in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Under the contract the Afghan military will receive 20 A-29s with the first batch being delivered in 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Pentagon has also proposed to provide to
      <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
       Lebanon
      </a>
      a contract for 10 EMB-314.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On September 2010, it was announced that Brazil and
      <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">
       United Arab Emirates
      </a>
      were working in a deal which includes sales of Super Tucanos.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was reported in early 2015 that UAE is negotiating with Embraer the purchase of 24 Super Tucanos, the deal would include 6 aircraft from Brazilian Air Force inventory for immediately delivery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 2011 the
      <a href="/wiki/Guatemalan_Air_Force" title="Guatemalan Air Force">
       Guatemalan Air Force
      </a>
      requested credit approval of $166 millions to buy six EMB-314, control centers, radar and equipment, in the context of a programme named "C4I".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In September 2012, the president of Guatemala stated that Super Tucanos will arrive within a year and half.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the following month, the Guatemalan Congress approved a loan for the C4I programme, including the purchase of six Embraer A-29 Super Tucano, to be granted by Brazilian and Spanish banks (BNDES and BBVA).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>

      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first two aircraft were expected to arrive in April 2014, followed by 2 units in 2015 and 2 more in 2016.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>

      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>

      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>

      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unasur" title="Unasur">

      </a>
      treaty, stating that it could promote the surveillance integration in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" title="Amazon Basin">

      </a>

      <a href="/wiki/Embraer_EMB_312_Tucano" title="Embraer EMB 312 Tucano">

      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KAI_KT-1" title="KAI KT-1">

      </a>

      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">

        <span>

        </span>

        <span>

        <span>

     <p>
      On October 2009, the President of Paraguay was leaning toward buying Super Tucanos.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>

        </span>

      <i>

      </a>
