     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Missed_contracts">
       Missed contracts
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Missed contracts">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      After the USA ban on Czech aircraft
      <a href="/wiki/Aero_L-159_Alca" title="Aero L-159 Alca">
       Aero L-159 Alca
      </a>
      export on 7 August 2009, the
      <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">
       Bolivian
      </a>
      Defense Minister said they were considering six aircraft from Brazil or China with comparable role as the Aero L-159.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 9 October 2009, it was announced that Pakistan would be manufacturing six Chinese
      <a href="/wiki/Hongdu_JL-8" title="Hongdu JL-8">
       K-8
      </a>
      for Bolivia, and to be used for anti-drug operations at the price of $9.7 million per aircraft.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On February 2006, a 36 unit sale for
      <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
       Venezuela
      </a>
      fell through because it was thought the USA would block the transfer of US-built components.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Venezuelan President
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hugo_Chavez" title="Hugo Chavez">
       Hugo Chavez
      </a>
      claimed the U.S. was responsible for pressuring Brazil not to sign the contract.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On November 2010 the President of the Legislative Defense Committee of
      <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">
       El Salvador
      </a>
      stated they will purchase estimated 10 EMB-314s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was postponed in February 2011 by lack of funds.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2013, the El Salvador Air Force acquired 10 Cessna A-37 retired from Chilean Air Force.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Elbit Systems and Embraer offered EMB-314 for the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      's basic trainer contest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the Beechcraft T-6C Texan II formed part of the preferred bid for the requirement in October 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Variants">
       Variants
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Embraer_EMB_314_Super_Tucano&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Variants">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       A-29A
      </dt>
      <dd>
       Single-seater for attack and armed
       <a href="/wiki/Reconnaissance" title="Reconnaissance">
        reconnaissance
       </a>
       (on interdiction tasks), attack and cover (on
       <a href="/wiki/Close_air_support" title="Close air support">
        close air support
       </a>
       tasks), able to intercept and destroy low performance aircraft. Incorporates an additional fuel tank (+ 400 liters).
      </dd>
      <dt>
       A-29B
      </dt>
      <dd>
       Twin-seater for the same tasks as the single seat version, also used in training and advanced aerial control (on monitoring tasks).
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Operators">
       Operators
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>

       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archive.defensenews.com_127-0">

          [
         </span>

         </span>

         <span>
          ]
         </span>

       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters-qua_161-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-reuters-qua-161">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         161
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In September 2012 it was informed that the country was in aprocurement process for acquisition of the type.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         162
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In April 2013, the Brazilian minister of Defence disclosed that Senegal is the 4th African nation to order the Super Tucano,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
        <a href="#cite_note-163">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         163
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the following day Embraer confirmed the order.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters-qua_161-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-reuters-qua-161">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         161
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       <span class="flagicon">
        <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
      </dt>
     </dl>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EP_Aviation_LLC" title="EP Aviation LLC">
        EP Aviation
       </a>
        part of
       <a href="/wiki/Academi" title="Academi">
        Academi
       </a>
       (formerly Blackwater)  at least one twin-seater variant for pilot training (delivered in February 2008), possible further orders for
       <a href="/wiki/Counter-insurgency" title="Counter-insurgency">
        counter-insurgency
       </a>
       role.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
        <a href="#cite_note-164">

         <span>

         </span>

         <span>

         <span>

         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.tacticalairsupport.com" rel="nofollow">
        [1]
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">
        United States Navy
       </a>
       leased an aircraft for testing, as part of the
       <i>
        Imminent Fury
       </i>
       program.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
        <a href="#cite_note-168">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         168
         <span>

         </span>

     <ul>
      <li>
       The first A-29 Super Tucano of the Pentagon's Light Air Support (LAS) program, destined for the Afghan Air Force, has been delivered to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Air_Force" title="US Air Force">
        US Air Force
       </a>
       in Jacksonville, Florida by the Sierra Nevada Corporation and Embraer in September 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archive.defensenews.com_127-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-archive.defensenews.com-127">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         127
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The LAS contract was developed by the Pentagon to supply Afghanistans military with 20 planes, which should ensure air superiority in the country after the majority of US forces leave. Because the contract is a foreign military sale, Nevada-based SNC and Brazil-based Embraer deliver the planes to the Air Force, which then passes them on to the Afghan military.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aviationweek.com_128-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aviationweek.com-128">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         128
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first of 20 A-29 Super Tucano aircraft arrived at
       <a href="/wiki/Moody_Air_Force_Base" title="Moody Air Force Base">
        Moody Air Force Base
       </a>
       on September 26, 2014 in preparation for the Afghanistan pilot and maintenance training mission.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
        <a href="#cite_note-169">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         169
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications_.28EMB_314_Super_Tucano.29">
       Specifications (EMB 314 Super Tucano)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>

       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Super_Tucano_FN_Herstal_M3P.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3456" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Super_Tucano_FN_Herstal_M3P.jpg/220px-Super_Tucano_FN_Herstal_M3P.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Super_Tucano_FN_Herstal_M3P.jpg/330px-Super_Tucano_FN_Herstal_M3P.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Super_Tucano_FN_Herstal_M3P.jpg/440px-Super_Tucano_FN_Herstal_M3P.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Super_Tucano_FN_Herstal_M3P.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Each wing can be loaded with 200 rounds for the
        <a href="/wiki/FN_Herstal" title="FN Herstal">
         FN Herstal
        </a>
        M3P 12,7 mm (.50 in) machine gun which has a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Firing_rate" title="Firing rate">
         firing rate
        </a>
        of up to 950 rounds per minute.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Super_TUcano_drops_bomb.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="495" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Super_TUcano_drops_bomb.png/220px-Super_TUcano_drops_bomb.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Super_TUcano_drops_bomb.png/330px-Super_TUcano_drops_bomb.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Super_TUcano_drops_bomb.png/440px-Super_TUcano_drops_bomb.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Super_TUcano_drops_bomb.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Pilots from the
        <a href="/wiki/81st_Fighter_Squadron" title="81st Fighter Squadron">
         81st Fighter Squadron
        </a>
        drop a 500 pound inert training bomb from an A-29 Super Tucano on the range near Moody Air Force Base, Georgia.

      <i>
       Data from
      </i>
      Type Analysis: Embraer Super Tucano (All specifications from Janes 2010-2011 unless otherwise indicated
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">

     <p>
      <span style="font-size: 120%;">
       <b>
        General characteristics
       </b>
      </span>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <b>
        Crew:
       </b>
       Pilot plus one navigator/student in tandem on Martin Baker Mk 10 LCX zero-zero ejection seats
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Payload" title="Payload">
         Payload
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       1,500 kg (3,307 lb)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Length:
       </b>
       11.38 m (37 ft 4 in)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Wingspan" title="Wingspan">
         Wingspan
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       11.14 m (36 ft 6.5 in)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Height:
       </b>
       3.97 m (13 ft 0.25 in)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Wing area:
       </b>
       19.4 m (208.8 sq ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Manufacturer%27s_empty_weight" title="Manufacturer's empty weight">
         Empty weight
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       3,200 kg (7,055 lb)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Maximum_takeoff_weight" title="Maximum takeoff weight">
         Max. takeoff weight
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       5,400 kg (11,905 lb)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_engine" title="Aircraft engine">
         Powerplant
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       1 Hartzell 5-blade constant speed, fully feathering, reversible-pitch 
       <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney_Canada_PT6" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney Canada PT6">
        Pratt &amp; Whitney Canada PT6A-68C
       </a>
       turboprop, 1,196 kW (1,600 shp) each
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      <span style="font-size: 120%;">
       <b>
        Performance
       </b>
      </span>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/V_speeds#Regulatory_V-speeds" title="V speeds">
         Maximum speed
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       590 km/h (319 knots, 367 mph)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/V_speeds#Vc" title="V speeds">
         Cruise speed
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       520 km/h (281 knots, 323 mph)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Stall_(fluid_mechanics)#Stall_speed" title="Stall (fluid mechanics)">
         Stall speed
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       148 km/h (80 knots, 92 mph)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <i>
         g
        </i>
        -limit:
       </b>
       +7/-3.5
       <i>
        g
       </i>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Range_(aeronautics)" title="Range (aeronautics)">
         Range
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       720 nmi (827 mi, 1,330 km)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Combat_radius" title="Combat radius">
         Combat radius
        </a>
        :
       </b>
       550 km (300 nmi, 342 mi) (hi-lo-hi profile, 1,500 kg (3,300 lb) of external stores)

         </span>

         <span>

        </a>
       </sup>

        </a>
        :
       </b>
       1,541 nmi (1,774 mi, 2,855 km)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-embraerpdf_172-0">

       </sup>

       <b>

        </a>

        <a class="external text" href="http://www.cjvanderende.com/publications/7" rel="nofollow">
         "Chile  Falces da Cordilheira" (in Portuguese).
        </a>
        Revista Asas Ed. 59, pp.3849.
       </li>
      </ul>
